Now the reason this is not entirely straightforward is that probability distributions and probability density functions are not arbitrary functionsã€‚

 for example a negative value and we know that probabilities cannot be cannot be negative so if we take an arbitrary neural network let's say call it a theta the output might be negative so we have to somehow change the structure or the neural network to make sure that the output is not negative and that's relatively easy to do for example we can take an exponential or something like that to make sure that the outputs are non negativeã€‚

The more complicated constraint is that we need to make sure that if we sum the probabilities of all possible inputs to this functionã€‚

 we sum the probability over all possible imagesï¼Œ we get oneã€‚

And enforcing this normalization constraint is not easy in order to make sure that this function normalizedã€‚

 we basically have to divide by this normalizedizing constant this dataã€‚

 which is just the integral of the unnormalized probability of all possible inputsã€‚

And this object is easy to compute if you have something simple like a Gaussian distributionã€‚

And the interesting thing is thatã€‚As we'll see this will allow us to define a very flexible class of models allow us and will allow us to directly bypass the issue of the normalization constant at the same time it will allow us to get very high quality images and this is kind of like the technology behind a lot of the advances that we've seen in generative models of imagesã€‚

 video speech and so forthã€‚And it will allow us to do a number of interesting other application built on top of generative models like evaluating probabilities doing outlier detectionã€‚

And that's going to be the score model and this is kind of like the key innovation that has allowed us to use more powerful neural networks to develop probabilistic models of imagesã€‚

Nowï¼Œ the question is that when we're given some training dataã€‚

 and we want to estimate the underlying vector field of gradesã€‚So it turns out that this can be doneã€‚

Through data generating process at that pointã€‚And what we can do is we are going to try to find parameters for these neural networks so that this function approximates the true vector field of gradients as well as possibleã€‚

Nowï¼Œ in order to do thatï¼Œ we need to be able to compare the modelã€‚

 the vector field obtained by the model to the vector field to the ground truth vector fieldã€‚

And so you can imagine that there is a ground truth vector filled those scoresã€‚

How do we compare these two objectsï¼ŸA reasonable thing to do is to basically overlap the two vector fields at every point there is going to be a truearrowã€‚

We can average them and we get scalar valueï¼Œ which is capturing how similar these two objects areã€‚

Mathematicallyï¼Œ this is known as the fis divergenceã€‚

And it's a reasonable metric to compare to vector field of scoresã€‚

The question is that it looks like it's a quantity that we don't know how to evaluateã€‚

Of course we don't know how to optimize because it depends on this ground truth vector field of gradients that we don't know we only have access to samples from the data distributionã€‚

 the goal is to estimate that through the ground truth data scoreï¼Œ how can we evaluate this quantityã€‚

Turns out that if you do integration by partsï¼Œ you can basically rewrite this objective function into an equivalent form up to a constantã€‚

And so now this is a reasonable objective function and the challenge is that it still depends on this trace of the Jacobbianã€‚

 which is potentially expensive to compute when we're dealing with high dimensional data the trace of the Jacobbian is basically a sum of partial derivatives with respect to the different input dimensions and this might require a lot of back propagation passes through the network in order to be able to evaluate this quantity exactly luckly there are several ways to approximately compute this quantityã€‚

One that I like is basically the idea of instead of comparing the vector field of gradients directlyã€‚

Larger number of different directionsï¼Œ then this should become a pretty good approximationã€‚

And by comparing random projectionsï¼Œ we're now comparing basically one dimensional objectsã€‚

And this leads to an objective function that' is much more computationally efficientã€‚

It basically does not depend on the dimensionality of the data anymoreã€‚

And it still retains a lot of the nice properties score matchingã€‚

 like consistency and a synthetic normalityã€‚I'm going to skip some of the detailsã€‚

And that connection arises if we start thinking about what happens if we were to consider a infinite number of noise levelsã€‚

Or recall that theã€‚Underlying idea of this modeling framework is to not just model the data distributionã€‚

 but to model the data distribution perturbed with increasingly large amounts of noiseã€‚

And here I'm showingï¼Œ let's sayï¼Œ the data distribution p0 and then several perturbed views of the data distribution and increasingly large amounts of noisesã€‚

Fine grain sort of set of perturbedã€‚Dta distribution perturbbed with different amounts of noise intensitiesã€‚

And in particularï¼Œ you can think about what happens if you were to consider an infinite number of noise distributions that interpolate between the clean data distribution at time zeroã€‚

So you can kind of like imagine there is a sequence of distribution where we start with clean data on the leftã€‚

And so in particularï¼Œ you can kind of like imagine process that kind of likeã€‚

Behaves according to this set of distributions marginallyã€‚

And you can kind of think about what happens if we were to take clean dataã€‚

And perturb it by adding increasingly large amounts of noiseã€‚

Until the structure in the data is completely destroyedã€‚

This can be described the stochastic process can be described by a simple differential equationã€‚

 stochastic differential equation where we basically just take data and add a little bit of noise at every step until after adding a sufficiently large amount of noiseã€‚

 all the structure in the data is completely destroyedã€‚

It turns out that it's possible to think about the reverse processã€‚

Where instead of going from data to noiseï¼Œ we go from noise to dataã€‚

So instead of going from time zero to tï¼Œ we go from time t to zeroã€‚And if we go from noise to dataã€‚ğŸ˜®ã€‚

This reverse process is basically solving the problem of generating data for usã€‚

Going from noise to data is exactly the process of jet generative modelingã€‚

And the interesting thing is that the reverse process of going from noise to data can again be described by a stochastic differential equationã€‚

 it's not important that you understand exactly what these equations meanã€‚

 the important bit is that this reverse stochastic differential equation can be described in terms of the score functionã€‚

So once againï¼Œ if we can estimate the score functions of these data densities perturbbed with increasing the large amounts of noiseã€‚

 then we can describe the reverse differential equation that maps noise to dataã€‚

And that's essentially the connection with the diffusion modelsã€‚

 it turns out that if we use score matching to estimate the score functionsï¼Œ we can reverseã€‚

this stochastic differential equationï¼Œ and we can get now essentially a diffusion modelã€‚

Time is continuous now that we can use to generate samplesã€‚And I think I'm running out of timeã€‚

 but I'll briefly mention that this stochastic differential equation perspective is very helpful becauseã€‚

It allows us to use a lot of different techniques from the numerical numerical methods kind of literatureã€‚

In particularï¼Œ it's possible to use very fast solvers for essentially computing the solutions to these stochastic differential equationsã€‚

 where it turns out that it's possible to convert this to an ordinary differential equationã€‚

So where the process is no longerã€‚tochastic is deterministic again the ordinary differential equation depends on the score function and so to the extent that we can estimate the score functionã€‚

 we can define an ordinary differential equation that maps noise to dataã€‚

And we can use numerical methods to solve this differential mis skip thisã€‚

 but we can use this differential equation toã€‚Accceerate samplingã€‚

 we can try to solve this differential equation very efficiently using techniques from the numerical methods that have been developed over decades to solve ODEs fastã€‚

 for example we can coersely disreitize the timeax and kind of like take big steps achieving very high speed appss and comparable sample qualityã€‚

 then you can repeat this process manyï¼Œ many times recursively until you can essentially get a student model that can generate samples in one stepã€‚
